O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the final word on the science of medicine in its entirety, and I have brought it to an end through my explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete this treatise for you, which is part of the work by hand, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work by hand is well-established in our region and is entirely strange to all, it is a very difficult science and requires a great deal of skill, and is not delayed by the small descriptions in books of the ancient ones that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive it with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of explanations and declarations and abbreviations; and I will come with the shapes of the ferments of cauterization, and other instruments of the work with the addition of the declaration and preparation of it, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because good masters of hands are not found in our times, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who deals with this to surmount in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so much that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations of bones, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of joints, and the movement and resting places, and the location of their exits.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because Hipocrates says that the less with the more is the work, and the work with the hand, and most of all in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not aware of the things mentioned above, let him not try to do anything so that he does not make a mistake and does not harm people; therefore, I have often warned many of those who deal with this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess on the neck of a woman, and also cut the arteries in her neck; for so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took out a piece of the bladder and the man died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have also seen a patient called for surgery, and saw the dislocation of the disease and the size of the stone, and he would surely die if it were removed.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who took a duc from our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was also a wound; and the doctor of ignorance pulled the break on top of the wound with great pain, and left no scar on the wound, and ended so; and he commanded that it should not be removed; and it delayed so that the leg was all rotten and the feet came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I did so, he was at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of corruption were already established in that member, and it cannot be healed; and the corruption does not cease to spread through the member as long as the members are all lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another mirage that would turn into an abscess, then it would inflame from the evil of its own essence.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For leprosy, when it is purulent with melancholy humor, never comes except that one touches it with iron in a place where it can be all removed what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And because, poor son, you need to know that work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, work in which there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For so that it may please you to take care of yourself, that the foolish mirth cannot speak ill of you; If you take your weapons in harmony, and undertake your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that, through the grace of God, you come to salvation and be loosed; and leave the possible diseases of grief health; and keep your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiénus then says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on yourself the care of a bad illness lest you be called a foolish mirth.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and water-based medicine, and the following chapters are ordered from the top down to the bottom; and the forms of the instruments, and the ironing tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters deal with dissection and perforation, suction cups and wounds, extraction of arrows, and similar things; the chapters also describe the order and shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and torments, and similar things; it also provides details on the preparation of the shoulder blades and the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, we must remember the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of help and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest word and subtlest science and its answers hidden; and many wise men would speak about it, and agree with what I say; and I am short of words because I shorten the long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire cautery helps all colors of skin where there is matter; for in one color there is heat and matter, and in another dry matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together matter, some agreed and said that cautery was great help; and the other said the opposite: that cautery is not worth anything to disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be cured by hot disease from heat, nor from dryness; and he who spoke the opposite said that cautery was great help to a hot and dry disease that comes in with men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all way, there is none who knows it but he who has tried it, and who knows by long practice the composition of the cautery, and the variety of complexions in men, their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their remedies and the space of time; otherwise we have no fear even for cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of this will come together and agree with the cauterizing.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery is more effective if it is applied to the open wound, and it has greater power than cautery with a hot tool.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is burned, and harms no other member by mistake.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The hot medicines come from one member to another by moving away, and cause diseases of great pain in the member; and fire, because of its height and power of its substance, does not hurt unless it is in excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experience and from the long service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I beg your pardon for the length of the speech, for I do not like to keep you waiting, but please accept in your thoughts the secret that is revealed through fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in his arguments; so receive it.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made in what time they must be done, and let them be prayed.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, for since the resulting harm can be prevented by the aid of cauterization; and most importantly, the cauterization is done because of the necessary pains that cannot wait for the time when greater harm does not come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think as some fools do; because the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they think, for cauterization is only a medicine that changes the appearance, and dries up the humors that cause pain; and it is better than medicine in terms of its speed in bringing about healing, and due to its virtue and nobility.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And a possible thing is that the disease comes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of meat and similar things, unless cauterization is administered at the place where he has little superfluity and moisture, as cauterization of the deep due to pain, and similar things, and partial pain does not return again; but it happens a little.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And so open well, for fire cauterization is the medicine of derriers, not because of the intention of foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And so open well, for fire cauterization is the medicine of derriers, not because of the intention of foolish men. The ancient ones said that cauterization instruments made of gold are more effective than those made of iron, and they said that the heat of gold and its high quality are what make them useful; they also said that the heat of a gold cautery does not cause scarring, but this is not true because I have tested it, and I have found that in some people it does cause scarring; and a gold cautery heals faster than an iron one, as they used to say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And however, when you heat an instrument made of gold, you will not recognize it by the color of gold, and it soon cools down; and if you heat it too much, it goes out on fire; and in this way there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you should read this chapter up to the point where the vision becomes clearer so that you can more easily find the way.
dou cautere olivaire	the olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery is useful for moist and cold conditions of the head, especially in cases of "soda" disease and various humors that descend from the scalp, ears, and a multitude of headaches and pains in the teeth and jaw, as well as similar diseases caused by cold, such as paralysis, sodiness, apoplexia, and other similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the disease should be expelled by a solitive medicine that rinses the head three or four times, depending on the virtue and acuity and the patient's accustomedness to it so as to endure it; and then rinse the head of the patient again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the crossbar between your hands, and put his hands on some meat; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his II eyes; and leave your two ends, if it bleeds, then heat the cautery which is called "olive", by which there is this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then place the crossbar between your hands, and put his hands on some meat; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his II eyes; and leave your two ends, if it bleeds, then heat the cautery which is called "olive", by which there is this form:
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And said the old man, that the longer the wound remains open, the more it seeps; and for this reason if the wound is treated promptly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said none of them that one must let the cauterize so long that part of the bone is burned, and then reset what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And said another that one must let the cauterize so long on, and press so hard that one takes off of the bone as much as women put in their brassieres to get rid of humors; and one must let the wound remain open for a long time; after it must be cured and treated.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good in all cases, except in certain men who have a tendency to fear; and it seems to me that I should let them remain open; for the head is weakened by continued solutions of nature, as we see with other members; and moreover, when the head of the ill person is weak by nature, and the first application of cauterization is more safe and gentle on mine, and of this I use to operate in a way that helps to save it.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the child's pain from head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the entire head is in pain and it lasts for a long time, then one should use herbes and pills that are called "cochia", and head-washing and oils and poultices; and if one does the fire cautery that we have mentioned above, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the head of the patient is of strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then cauterize him only a little as we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made the fire cautery over each of the patient's horns as we have said above, and you have made a hole at the base thereof, so that one can put leeches there; and place the leeches therein; and place your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary that the horn cauteries be made narrower than those by which one cauterizes the skin of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	A fire cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain in one side of the neck occurs and persists up to the oil, and the shoulder is dislocated by medicines that cause fever, and the other cures I mentioned in the division of diseases do not help: then make two kinds of cauterizations, namely with water medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with water medicine is done as follows: You squeeze a piece of aloes, and then remove the skin and cut it in two pieces, and then apply it to the shoulder in the form of a temple or band where the pain persists, so that you can put back the aloes on the skin; and when it has been re-applied, let it rest for twelve hours; and then remove it and treat with garlic oil, leaving the wound open for two or three days; then apply cotton dipped in wax until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of ointment as long as he is healthy; and if you see that this one of some burning medicines that I have written or dozed out in the doctor of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if it is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer so that it is hot:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "clos" because the head is made in the form of a clod or there is a little curve, and put it on top of the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, so that half of the burn wound is burned; and remove your hand so that the artery does not hurt, which is hot, and run a lot of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in silk, and put it on the spot for three days; then I put wet cotton in butter, and then treat the sore place with ointment as long as it is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cauterizer that is called "cultellare", at the very tip, and beware of sealing the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of headaches
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	For headaches: When you treat headaches as we have said before in the division of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cauterization before mentioned with medicine and iron does not suit him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and so mark on the painful spot a line of half a finger long, and raise your hand once, and draw back so that you do not cover the artery and do not come up to the bone; and guard against the mandible that moves when it is bitten, and let rest only that which is mute and that spasms do not come to the disease, and guard against the release of blood from the artery when it is covered, or when it has been covered with great fear and mostly by those who do not know, and who are students and untested; and leave the work in half a way; but I will tell you how to stop headaches when the artery is covered, and I will show you at what point it takes effect in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice to the disease, and the patient suffers, cauterize him with fire on the top of the head as well, and cure the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautery which we have said or the extract of the artery with the cautery having two knives; and this cautery is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ears from cold, and one has applied soluble medicines and other treatments which we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then apply this fire which is called "poins," of which form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying fire to the entire ear that hurts, or to both sides where the pain is felt at the root of the ear, and keep it burned for X minutes; then treat the area until it heals.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	that must be cured by fire is only of those that move with a stream, as we have said in the divisions of the diseases; and not to make any fire on similar things that come from thirst and spam of blood.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this torture of the mouth that moves with a stream of fluid from the throat and gargling, and not worth it, then you must make three fire treatments: one in the root of the ear, another about a finger further away from the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips; and place the fire on the part that is healthy, and let the fire burn halfway; and this is the form of the fire:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the appearance of the scalpel that we have put before you is a little more delicate, and it is necessary that the knife be a little thicker; after healing, keep it as I said above until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexies are old and you treat them in this way as we have said, they do not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations: II on the two horns of the head, and I cut off the head, and I put it in a pot as we have said before, and a cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be cured in this way as we have said above.
de litargie	of limestone
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient great years and pills to take away the brain; after healing the whole head of the patient, and put on his occiput a plaster of saffron which is written or treated plasters; and this is the way of the cauterization: if you do so as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healthy then it is good, and if not, he does three fire cauterizations on the top of his head down to the collarbone, and there should be space between each cauterization of two inches in width; and treat him as you would the others, and if he appears to struggle, the patient suffers, so do one in the middle; and if it is necessary, do two more on either side of the two horns, and treat him until he is well, and the cauterizations that are called "olive-wraps" should be done as I have said above.
de la froidor dou chief	of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed with dirt and water as we have said above; after washing the head of the patient, then he does a fire cauterization on top of his head and one on each horn, and one behind and three along the spine of the neck; and if you need to, and the cors is moist and the patient suffers and is getting worse, do three cauterizations on the spine of the back; and let it be until the fire has burned the skin of the last cauterization, and lift your hand; after treating him until he is well, and the cauterizations that are called "olive-wraps" as we have said above.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Of the epileptic, should only use fire cautery who is fluent, and first to wash the brain of yarrows and other cures that we have said in the division when the illness is great and suffering from poison medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot bear the poultice, let him gargle and chew washing the brain often with good meat; after that he places his head in the middle, and does the poultice according to what we have said before, and the poultice on the neck, and each horn; and if the illness is fierce and suffering, do the poultices as I have said to those who are paralyzed and weakened of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the poultices be olive according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, make the fire cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, there are excesses or corrusions and thick pus, then make the cautery partly as we have said above for those who are paralyzed.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, there is excess decline towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him to drink something to clear his mind, according to what it says here about it before the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cutting off the head of the patient; after making a well-formed tortue out of linen, also as a circle, if you put it around his head; and let the patient sit still and be held down well on all sides; then present the linen, and dip it in good bee wax; and heat it gently by fire so that he can bear it; then empty the circle out from inside the head and let it cool down; and do this to the patient every week once with another good government, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see, to cauterize them by making dots everywhere with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This way of cauterizing dries out the brain as well; and then put on cotton wet with linseed oil and with sheep's-fat grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the hair
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes to the hair, first of all, according to the signs that I mentioned in the division, then begin and do this for the patient, purifying the brain, and warding off all moisture, and making him sweat or bath several times while fast.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, he orders him to re-set his hair, and he makes him sweat or bath several times while fast. After it has been set, he makes II cauteries on the II temples where it is dislocated from the hair, together, or if it is dislocated in one place, then it is set there; and guard against bleeding from the scalp, and if you see too much blood coming out, then restrain him so that he cannot move.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you how to cauterize during the extraction of arteries and the incision, how to stop it; and no one does cauterization or dismemberment of the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	The heart's blood
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or squeeze the arteries which are in appearance at the base of the head; and one can see that it is of the cold and phlegmatic surplus, therefore I do the cautery that I said at the beginning of the chapter descending to the tears: I cauterize the top, and two cauterizes on the two temples, and two cauterizes where haters dismember the two bones; and if it is necessary more, if he cauterizes well on the temple a little cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The heart's blood from inside the tears
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you prepare the medicine as we have said in the division, and it does no good, then done three times take a drink of the disease; after that he raises his head, and makes a cautery with oil of olive in the middle; and make two cauteries with the cautery which is called "clavis" on the two scars, a little hair-cutting; and guard the artery so you don't cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery with this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	so that you know this form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you do two cauteries on the two scars as long as the scars are; and don't let your hand off until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	with hair that points to oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has passed that the hair of the oils have been turned into the parched lands, and they touch the oil, and it is done on two ways: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so that they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient on your table; afterwards sign on the paper of the hairs a figure that is also like the furrow of the mirth, and this is the beginning of the sign to pluck the hairs; then put cotton wet in wax and muskellaige (a type of resin) on the oil, then heat the cautery so that it has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cauterized the wound little by little several times, so that the scar is burned in place; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retire, and the hairs stand up at the point of the oil; then lighten your hand, and leave it like this for III days, then put cotton wet in lard until the chapping is healed; after the cure of the wound until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after these come the hairs, and the paper is softened then start again the fire on this same place, as you have done first; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural position, and even, and does not touch the hair the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical fire cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a roll of parchment in the shape of a fern; then take French soap and very hot water, each a .z., and grind them together well; and do it quickly, so that it doesn't cool down, then pour it over the roll of paper; and if the illness holds only in one oil, then do it also with another; and dip the cotton wet in lard into an oven; and the patient's joints are in your hand and put your thumb on the medicine, and press it a little and move it all the time that the patient feels tingling from the medicine, for he feels tingling also as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	Once you have learned this lesson well, keep the medical treatment at your side.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blister has passed, lift up the bandage, and you will see the paper raised as if it were lifted by fire or incision; and if so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, put the medicine back on the place where the medicine has not worked, as long as your hair is long and even, and your eyes are in place; then put cotton soaked in vinegar on it until the burns are healed, after treating the injury that is called "diaphoresis" and others, as long as it is healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must bandage yourself well so that the medicine does not touch your hair.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft after it, and the hair pricks in the oil, then repeat the medicine on that same place that has been softened by the paper properly, as you have done before; after treating until it is healthy; and this is the form of the poultice of mint:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and height, and according to this, their constraints; and do not be answered with the right path to those whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit them, then it is appropriate that you make a cauterization according to this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient that he put his head in your clean; and wet the minsters of his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, do not shake his head; after dip cotton wet in wine or juice of pease on oil; after heat the cautery which is good: and place upon the head like the form of a goose feather, together that the lip is the cautery; if you see, then join one head to the other, and if you see, so too as an umbrella; but nevertheless, it who is placed is moved for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula is opened, and treat the pus, and dry it up; and if it has closed, so work on it, and firmly grasp the scar tissue with your hand below the oil, that your hands do not go mad; and place the cauterizer in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then start cauterizing again, and do so as many times as you need to, and leave it for III days; after that put cotton soaked in grease on the wound, and dry out the healing with a drying medicine for as long as it is healthy, and if forty days have passed and it is still not healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat according to the chapter on this.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have a way of cauterizing fistulas, which no one of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Do you understand a fistula, and pierce it; then put in the slender tool with which this is done:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I pour the quantity of one.Z. of wine; and hold your hand firmly where the cautery is, so that the molten wine does not run to its oil; and it comes that you put on the cotton soaked in water or in ale to: the wine if artfully applied to the fistula, and it is cured per marvelously health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is cured by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	But if not, then let him give a blow to the nose, and bring back the fistula to the root of the nose according to what one should do in his own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Mouth times have cracks in the lips that are called "hair", and most often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks from what we have said in divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then warm a small surgical cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it directly in the cracks as long as it comes out clean; after treating with oil, let it dry up until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes at the root of the throat or in the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after having made a poultice and wrapped it and it becomes dry and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit: then it is appropriate that you have a cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after the boil or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron comes out at the bottom of it, and do so once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, as long as it is healthy; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, then it is appropriate to uncover the site and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	dou movement des dens
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and this does not work, then put the head of the sick person in your lap; then heat the cautery whose shape will come later in a certain way that you place a cord on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and start again with the cautery according to your will; then fill the mouth of the sick person with salt water, and let it sit for an hour and wash it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a certain way the tooth that was moving is fixed, and the gums softened are restrained, and the moisture dries up and腐敗。
de la dolor des dens	of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or it is cold or wet, and medicines do not work, then there is a need for two kinds of cauterization: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter if it is such that you squeeze butter from a cheesecloth, and the tip into a copper or bronze spoon; after take cotton and wrap around the tip of a tent, and soak it in butter, and put on the tooth aching slowly and hold so long as it cools down; and thus often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and see if this butter, cotton and cotton wet is cold, and put on the tooth aching, and put on I copper hot as the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Cautery with fire if it is such that you squeeze a piece of iron or bronze, and make it thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heat the cautery, for then the shape will come out later, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be sharp on the following day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the hurry of this cautery, and then drink it down; and thus is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cauterized wound on the back of the neck, and according to what you can; and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of a cold, moist flu and does not respond to digestive medicines, then heat the scalp with fire in order to prepare it, and after that comes the form: and make two openings for the fumes to exit on either side; and put the fire on the abscess once, where it belongs, until it reaches the root of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply fire according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it like that for three days; and put cotton wet with butter on it as long as the burning is over; then treat with oils and poultices until he is well.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails over the jaw, and most often when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be voided by restorative medicines; afterwards he makes the cautery at the root of the throat, and you should not go up to the throat, and do not cut off anything but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards he makes another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let be the cauteries which are called 'claws' so that we have the form before; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the tongue
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the disease of the jaw is due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or scorbutic disease, and it is an old illness, then he makes iij cauteries on the face according to the form which is before said; and another cautery goes down between the breasts. And let be the cauteries which are called 'claws' according to the form which is before described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make the fire cautery by puncturing all the cauterizations that are called "poins" of which the shape is as described above in the disease of the ears; and let the punctures be up to 30 or so.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards treat the wound according to what is said above, and let the cauterization be made in three layers according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for those for whom the cauterization is lighter, make three of them together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards let the patient lie on his back and on his chest; then with the two fingers of your left hand reach inside the ear; and if the joint moves inwardly, then apply the fire cauterization in two layers according to this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize it as far as it pierces to the cost, and comes the shape of the cautery together with four cauterizes; and because it is done cauterization with the cautery which has three nerves, because the figure of cauterization are there cauterizes; and the nerve according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cautery which has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And no time is placed on this nerve because there are eight cauterizes.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After put on the cautery, grind it with salt; after let rest the patient, and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, what happened there, then make cauterize on the thick of the cautery clave, or more than cauterizes in piercing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and the moisture is dried up, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come coldness and moisture until it is taken away from its color, and there are many catarrhs to him, and the customs of the usual cures do not benefit him, then the patient should be swaddled around his body, and his legs and hands spread out.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From then on he will make three cauterizations of the navel with fire, all cauterizations being clamped down, and two cauterizations along the sides as long as the shape of the cauterization is at three angles, and there should be a space between each of them so that they are not joined together when they burn; and may the shape of the cauterization be perfect so that it burns the two parts equally, and may the shape of the cauterizations follow this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you want to cauterize your stomach with a large fire, according to this form; and he who is afraid of this fire, cauterize by puncturing and pressing on the stomach in one point according to the quantity that you see fit, then cauterize it with all the fire that is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the healing process that we have described above, until he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, it suffers from cold and moisture and strong wind, until it is separated from its natural composition due to excesses; and the patient is treated in accordance with what we have mentioned in the divisions, and it does him no good unless he becomes tired of his own evil; and sign of a line III cauterizes according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, leaving a space between each cauterize the size of two fingers; and let the cauterize be as long as the back of the neck, and do not press too much with your hand at all the cauterize; and let it be burned so intensely that half of it is consumed, and let the patient lie on his back; and if he cannot, then let him extend his legs, and raise his breasts; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is, then cauterize these cauterizes of the cutlet, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the cure, for you would dry out all the body; and let it come no further than a pimple, for the cure is very subtle in place, and the saiges to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you can discern whether it is in the parenchyma of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the parenchyma, then feel that the patient feels little pain; and if it is in the capsule, then feel severe pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure has finished with the pus, it is necessary that the patient should be attentive to his head; and then sign with your finger where the abscess is, and then heat the cauldron which resembles the tip, from which comes:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I cauterize until the fever is burnt, and come to syphac, as long as the poultice is all wet; after the cure according to the cure of the sweats until he is healthy; and it is not convenient that this cautery use any wet but those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by which these diseases have been corrupted no time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And now he can dare to work, and always it seems to me that he leaves it too long;
dou cautere de pleuresin	Dou cauter of pleurisy:
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make a cauterization for pleurisy with roots of arzilla, and in this way: take a root of arzilla that is long, the largest you can find, dry it, and also make it as thick as your two hands; and moisten it with oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize between the nipple and the collarbone, and three small cauterizations a little lower down on the side that is sore; and one cauterization under the breast, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and one along both sides of the chest after the fire has gone out; and do not press your hand tightly, but rather open it widely as if you were smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no old man uses fire cautery like a razor, and he blows it and puts it between the ribs until it comes to the stump; and he jumps out of pain, as we have said in the incision of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes out which cannot be healed.
de la mice	for the mercy
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of mouse-poison which we have said in the division of cures, and it does not help, then they have devised three kinds of fire cautery which are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
