S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If the subtle poison is there, and it is close to the lips, if you hurry, and then turn her; put your two fingers together, and the woman on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two lips, as long as the subtle poison remains, and the stooping is covered; then take wool, and wet it with oil, and put it on the spot, and lay the woman on her back every day, so that he cannot hold it.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the remedy is harsh and bitter, it is necessary that you take with the spatula a substance resembling a leaf of myrrh.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the stinging is of fire, then hang it on the thistle and cut it; and apply the medicines that stop the pain, as has happened before, pain of dragon, incense, a mixture of ash; and then introduce a large piece of pluck, so that the wound cannot close; and thus let it be for a long time, and introduce a sheet of dry linen; and so cure with other remedies until it is well.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the wound on the arm comes to be of fire, if it is necessary to cover it according to this method, let it not be infected with abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For at an abscess infected that is in the arm, one must not touch fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	of hemorrhoids are openings of veins whose custom is without treatment, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become thorny; and we have said in the division the appearances of ears, and signs, and I will say here those who receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thorns, when they are perfect in the pelvis, and do not appear by touch, but only by cure with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the entrance of the pelvis, one can feel them, are those who can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then bind the thorns to the sheath, and insert the cope into her roots, then powder with medicines restraining blood, as we have done, and blood of dragon and incense, and similar things; then pour its feet on the wall for an hour, then let her sit in cold water; and if the pain comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confit with honey, and apply it as a poultice to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it has stopped, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if it doesn't, you must blow on the back and massage without hurting; then take another, and the juice of plantain or of acacia with old wine, and blow at the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has subsided, you must keep the wound clean until it is healed; and that which is called "balath" is red, and looks like a sharp stone, so cover it as I have said before; and then keep it clean until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	The abscesses of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Come in the breast many ways of abscess come, like cancer and painful abscess and herpes and estiomens and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I die in this treatise on the abscess that comes to the breast, which is not an abscess that burns, and if you know the work of iron, then consider that the abscesses are fresh when they begin to come out, full of heat and fever, and if they turn red, you can see them.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So then you should not hurry to pierce it, but let it die until the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit down on two small chairs or pillows so that their legs are apart from each other; and their knees spread, and tie them firmly with a good cord; then suck the bile towards the left side of the chest, and bring the instrument with which you operate on the mouth of the breast, after which comes the shape; and it is necessary that when you introduce the instrument into the breast, you insert it as deeply as it should and not more, so that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover its depth with drapes, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top of it, and wrap it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et when the abscess is opened, and one holds it in the hand, if it is convenient to cover the head, let the sputum flow; and when the bowels are empty, if it is convenient that you put into the wound tents wet with oil of roses or with oil of green herbs; place the tent completely outside the wound at the bottom of the mare, and on the other side of the hand clean it with water or burned malva; then cure after two days of poulticing coming to this, until he is healed; and never raise the mare and the wound by means of a cup of water and honey, and then only of water or roots of licorice and long-rooted herbs are cooked; then bring back the poultice.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is covered with the mare, keep yourself from cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	For the art of midwifery, it is first necessary that she knows the natural shape of childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman rushing downwards, and desiring to smell the air: then the baby's head comes out; then you know that these childrens are according to the natural shape, and the issue is with its head, and the second one with it; and when you see these signs, then you should gently press her belly, so that the baby comes soon; for when he descends on his head, then the second one comes with him, and the husband is cleansed of his excesses by good purification; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes never but upon its feet, and comes from the neck or shoulder, or hands, or sometimes comes up its belly, or oft, and is turned round by accident on its throat, and in other evil shapes; therefore it is necessary for midwifery that she be wise and skilled in these things, and ward off error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how to help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If a man falls on his head because of natural cause and the woman gives birth with great pain, and the virtue of him is weak, so that she puts it on a saddle, or the women hold it; and he rises from the oil or fenugreek which is cooked, and then pours the wine between her two little nipples in this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If a man falls on his head because of natural cause and the woman gives birth with great pain, and the virtue of him is weak, so that she puts it on a saddle, or the women hold it; and he rises from the oil or fenugreek which is cooked, and then pours the wine between her two little nipples in this shape: and splits the second one, and ties his nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and rubs the woman's belly with muscillaige of fenugrec with oil of sesame; then makes her rub and shake off the condescension, and keeps her mouth and nose closed for an hour: then now the baby.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, it is necessary that you pull them gently a little and a little; and if they cannot enter, let the woman sit on a chair, and lift her feet up; then take off the chair from the ground, and tie the woman so that she does not fall down; and if the hands cannot enter, and the baby dies, if he pushes his hands with the knife that is placed in front, and pulls out the child, and leaves it even.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	and of the delivery of the child at its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out at its feet, then it is necessary to turn it up; and then pull it little by little until it is even; then squeeze its feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can't he jump just as soon as his legs come out, then instruct him to squeeze and make it vibrate with the hand; if he jumps, let God take care of him.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not turn out as we have said, if the shoulder becomes dislocated little by little until it is back in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light again.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	For then it is easy again. And if it does not turn out as we have said, if the muscle of the loins and the oil of sissament, and gum dissolved, and ground up in a mortar; and put on the nature of woman inside and take off this ointment, then let her sit in water until she is wet all over; and when she is wet all over, let her put the cologne of myrrh on, and put it on, and leave it for an hour; then let her sit down, then make her sneeze and strain her mouth and nose, and squeeze her belly lightly, because the baby jumps out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	the birth of the child between her legs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if he puts his bail his hands little by little; then be supported on his neck, and hang his feet down, and be lying on my bed; and he bends his hands little by little, and then he takes his hands on his belly, and lifts up his testicles with a bunch of grass, so that they are removed down; and if the child does not jump, if he takes his feet and moves them, then he moves his belly upstream, then I pour my hands; and the baby is little by little; and command to the woman that she prays as long as the child is.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The child's delivery, when it comes out wide, a hand holds him back.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	When the child's delivery is difficult, a hand supports him: if it cannot be supported, let the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, let her sit on the bed, and spread her legs wide; then I will bring the instrument mentioned earlier; and if she does not give birth, let her sit on a chair, then try to support the hand; and the child according to his natural form, and make him sneeze, and command that she prays as long as the child is.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa face tornee devers lou dos sa mere
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	As the child comes out of the womb, he will spread his hands and turn his face towards his mother's back. It is necessary that the midwife hold him gently, turning him little by little, and when he is straight, she places him on a bed, and tells her to move her hips gently; and when you have done this, if you put a pillow under his bottom, she will sit down, and tells her to move her hips, and let the child fall.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	from this middle manner at all the second time
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When he comes in this way at all the second time, if you tie his second foot so that the moisture is empty; and if he catches himself on his face and on his neck, so that he does not get stuck, and dies the child; then put the child inside again, as long as you have put it in the right way, and order the woman to move her hips lightly: and then if she does so slowly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born often, and only three or four times are born; and this is not a strange thing, and rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are an odd thing, and do not live, but one; I know that, if they are multiplied, and are devised by the physician who is tied to the bougie; and they are also born naturally as all others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	If they are born with pain, and the cure is as we have said, and if the doctor is subtle, and does quickly and lightly what he has to do; and does it well, so that he saves them.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No child is formed from one to fifteen, or more, up to seventeen, and they are all formed in the image of a child by the measure of the wise glory, and the doctor knows everything about them, for sometimes strange things happen; so he does it according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of a dead child or an abdomen, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work with your hands; if it is necessary that you know that the woman is of sound health, and has no accident which she might fear would kill her; if it is necessary that the woman be supported on her back, and her children are inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister rubs her with oil from both sides, or she lies in bed so that she cannot be treated for the descent of the child; then you rub the mouth of the pregnant woman with moist oils with althaea and fenugrec and flax seed, then you anoint the hands of the woman with these oils and these muscuraides; then you pour them into the woman lightly, then you want to pour them out where they can be suitable for what, and take care that the child is dressed in such a way that it descends on his head; then he pours the oil into his hair or col or mouth or throat or larynx or near the ribs, and the descent is on the feet, if he pours or pricks and cuts at the cost of the hands; and it is necessary that he dye the oil with his right hand, and puts the bowl between his two hands on his left, and pours it all lightly with his right hand, and pours the oil into any of the places I have said, until he comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the oil:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then take another piece of twine, or if you need it, so that the extractions are even; and then make them even by moving one way and another, so that they come out, and let the teeth of the oncines hold them, as this is their form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If one part stops, then oil two of its ends, and squeeze that part, and pull the other; and if none stop, then put this oncaine where it should be or higher up, and tie it so that all come out far away.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	If one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back by stretching, then you must wrap him in a blanket, all of it, then take the covering from the joint of the foot or the wrist, and do the same to his other hand, and to his feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l'enfant est gros et il est estrois en l'issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si convient que tu boute le spatumile espineux entre tes deux, et fent le chief et estrai l'aigue; ou tu la ront a l'estrument qui est apelez "almidach", de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cesti; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturellementment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s'elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pleux; et s'il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si convient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if it is trapped under its feet, then the slight pull is, and the treatment is light for the mouth of the horse.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is caught in the abdomen or breast, then cover it with a drape wrapped over your hand; and cut open the abdomen or breast until the moisture that is causing it comes out; and if another member has been dislocated and the joint remains stuck, then wrap your hand firmly around the mare's head, and pull gently; then I will saw one or two, and cut firmly; and if the mouth of the horse has become tight due to a hot abscess that has come, then it is not necessary to work, but only to soften and moisten things; and he softens them, and cuts them into water-softening and moistening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if it is caught on the ribcage, and you can make it even, then treat as we have said above for a live child; and if one does not have the power, then cut it into pieces, leaving nothing of the second one.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, bring the person who has said to us in the apothem that comes out in the water; and let them run away from blood coming, if it is stopped by restraint and let other treatments be brought.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose child had been killed, then another consulting about it, and another refusing to kill it.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, the ten apotomes in the bowl began to swell up, and started to rot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I could not stop the wound from bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong plaster, and in it went a bone, and after a few days others came out.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled very much, for this woman's belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	Then I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted to treat the wound, and in three hands, as long as the woman was in good shape; and she stayed there for a long time, and a little of the bone came loose from its place; and I did not remember this ointment before, except that when the master saw a strange thing, he knew how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the wife to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, so we set the bones; and at two turns are formed the two shoulders.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the ears should be thinner than the supports and made of ebony or box; and the mouth of the funnel must be wide, and the margin of the branches must be long, about a palm and a half; and these two supports are joined at their ends, each to its own, which are firmly fixed in the mouth of the wife to open when the horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, its appearance more subtle and lighter, shall be made of ebony or boxwood according to the appearance of the teeth; it should have two supports, as you see, a palm long and two fingers wide; and when you open the mouth of the woman entirely with the instrument, let her sit on the bed with her legs open and the feet hanging down, then put together the two supports onto the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument between her knees; then place your hand over the entire instrument as you did with the teeth evenly, according to the quantity that you open the mouth of the woman, until the ball comes out.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all mounted and has multiple uses; and when you see that they are prepared, the more quickly it is done, and the higher it is raised for its quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If I don't have an instrument, you have not prepared it, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second is retained at childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to keep her tongue between her teeth, and then make her sneeze by putting your hand on her belly and pulling down; and if she sneezes because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If he doesn't sneeze because of this, I can catch him, and make a trapdoor or lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the pregnant woman, as calamus, rue, anise, camomile, cassialine, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, are boiled or put in water over the fire; then put one corner or lid over the pot, and the other chief in the mouth of the pregnant woman, and hold it until the vapors come up inside the pregnant woman; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If jump the second time hospital.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If she remains after this cure and is not well, order her to moisten her left hand in olive oil or muscatel wine [muscellaige de altee], and then let it fall into nature, and let it hang; and when she has found it, if she grabs it and stretches it little by little correctly, so that the marrows do not break at extraction; but she must move it lightly from left to right, and then pull it out; and then she will take off her ring.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the marrow in her mouth is stiffly extracted, we have said the cure of vomiting, and fomentation of herbs; and if she does not do all that we have said, you must guard against making her vomit by forcing; but it is necessary that he who is in the mouth of the marrow, you bind him to the girdle of the woman, then let him enema with tetrafarmacon [a medicine consisting of four parts]; if she will and will come to health, but nevertheless, when she has done so, if a bad odor comes up to her stomach and head, and bleeds the sick person.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is appropriate then let there be suitable fumes for him: no one of the ancient ones has tried fuming with nettle and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument by which they fumes the woman at the retention of flowers and of the second one if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of a shape resembling a dog, and one puts the head soft in nature, and the shoulders wide on fire; and let the fumes be on the coals, and the hair until it is spent, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not yet had the foundation pierced, but it is pierced by a subtle syrup: if it is necessary then to let him pierce that subtle syrup at his right, and he does not pierce it with a spit, and seal the lancing so that it does not touch; then put on another moistened cloth in wine and oil, and the cure of ointment until it is well.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not return, so put a peg in a hole, and let his hands be free, and be oasted when he falls down to go into the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And there is no sudden return of the wound or abscess; if it is covered suddenly: if it is cured, as we have said above about the peg.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the fundament are nodulation, and more painful than those that come from the fundament or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, if it opens, and again moistens with a pale or subtle bow, and these fistulas never persist; and they are known by that which he has in excretion or venting when the sick person does so, and perhaps in a jump.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it pierces to the vesicle, and only up to half the length of the penis; and it reaches up to the juncture of the scrotum, and only up to the tip of the cow's udder.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so you will know if the fistula reaches to the perineum, and not further: and that you pierce your little finger or perineum, and pierce a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula when it does not have any curves.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has any curves, if you pierce with a fine thread of rope, or hair of a horse, as far as you feel the thread or hair on your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no perforation or wind-up or blood flow, as we have said: know that it does not hurt; but if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persisting until the bladder or until the urinary conduit, if there is urine leaking, and cannot be treated with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived only to the joint of the hip, if it is attempted coming up to the place; if there is no twistedness and the invention of the pain inside, if it is that he has already bowels, and cannot be treated with medicine or remedy by finger pressing; and in these persisting fistulas there is no cure but labor, and vanity of foolish mirages which enter into them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one which is not persisting and is not ancient, there is hope of health by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and let the legs go up to his hips, and bend his hips towards his belly; then pour a bucket of rain, or of water if there is twistedness, until you know where the fistula comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the fundament, then you should insert your index finger, you will feel that the tent is pierced; and if it is uncovered or you feel between your thumb and the syph, you know that it is persistent; if not, it does not work so that it can be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	If the patient experiences pain in the fundament, you should insert your index finger, and you will feel that the tent is pierced; and if it is uncovered or you feel between your thumb and the phlegm, you know that it is persistent; if not, it does not work so that it can be healed. Now I will explain how to treat some of them well, but this only works sometimes; and the aid that you give, if you heat the small cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said above; and pour it directly into the fistula, as many times as you feel that these charred things are burned, which look like a bird's feather; and then cure with wet cloth, until the char falls off, and then cure with ointment, binding the char and sealing it.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, then it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If then is so, it is good. But if not, he cannot be healthy; and if he tries to stand up, and does not pierce until at the root which is at the foundation, and has between his two feet a thick covering of cloth or of medicine, and you see the fistula at that covering where it begins; then the cope of the beginning of the fistula, and press forward again before the covering, and after cauterization, as long as it comes to the top of the covering; and will be delivered the covering, and he will be well; then I fear those covered cars which seem a feather of an owl, and there remains neither.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain does not go away, and presses between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or with medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: that is to say, the burning of these joints that are put together, and the cooling of blood and the drying of the moist; then cure the tents that are wet with a kind of mud or a dry thing, as long as they run down, and burn these cars in the mud; then cure the wound with medicines that are hard and dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it has been restored, so is healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the foundation, and is distant from the body, let it be broken at the foundation, and query this one.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	And if you feel the tent, and it is there the fabric or the syringe or the char, or it is ready to pierce, then there is only way of engagement and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it just to the foundation, or if you can put tents and cure it as first; and do not go too far in the perfection, so that you cover the tent which holds the foundation, and bring the effusions by the voluntary way; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the world then it is cut away from the foundation, or with a tent or another instrument pointed; then mend this rotten thing which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to delay the fistula in the part away from the foundation: it will be a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there are no times that are fists according to this way: and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or costs on the foundation of the delicate skin on top, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put two wires in two, and put the tent on all the wire in the fistula as long as it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing in the margin of the foundation within, then remove the wire from that one, so that you put your two at the foundation; and draw the head of the wire, and join together the two shoulders, and pull them apart, and leave them for a day or two; and do not hold back any time, as long as the wires cross those lines that are between two, and rub against each other; then cure the wound until it is sewed up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If it does not perforate, if you pierce it with all your might, it will not be too much.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make the wound tighter if it is already too tight, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healthy again.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spikelet from which one makes the fistula is so sharp that it pierces on one side and cuts on the other; and on this side it should not be tighter than on that side, so that it does not cause pain, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: they may be inside the fundament, like a grain of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and they may be tied together tightly; or they may be outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside have a little moisture, and sometimes a little blood, and they are red in color; and the cure for those inside the fundament is this: order the patient to strain himself by sitting on chambers until the fundament moves, and then let him go; if you hurry, and grasp them with your fingers, or hold them between your nails, then cut off their roots; and if they do not stay because of their moisture, catch them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of cloth; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them off, and powder them with hot powders that are for cauterizing; or cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery; because other cures do not cure them until they are healthy; and if the fundament cannot come out, then clisterize the patient with a clisterizing fluid that is harsh and sharp to wash out what is inside the fundament, so that it can come out freely; when the patient is strained, and the roots of the hemorrhoids have gone out from the fundament, then loosen them gently; and grasp them with your fingers or pliers, and cut them off, then cure them as we have said, until they are healthy, and let them avoid being incised with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you stitch in this way: take a tortuous thread, and bottle it in a needle, and then wind the thread around the top of the needle and pierce the other end through, and join the two ends of the thread at the needle's eye, and if they are wide apart; twist the thread into a form, then tie the knot, remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave it to drain off the blood; then put on the foundation a moistened cloth oiled with rosewater or wax, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he rest; and then let him remain as long as he is sewing, and when he has finished sewing, he is to be treated with ointment and other cures until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	to dry at the end or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying out at the end in the intestine, and by necessity of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is no longer effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you cut off the skin from a spit or your finger above it, which you do not leave to dry; then treat it until it is firm as it should be; and if it cannot be treated, then begin to shave it more severely than before, until it heals and is skinned; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	he will sweat
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	There is a small appearance of decay before the shoulder, and it swelters perfectly; and there is no pain when it is cut, and one can feel it everywhere like death from sweating, and it spreads all over the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a string from an ostrich egg, or a strong vulture feather, and put that string on the sweating, until the purple circle covers the sweating all around; then turn your hand to hold all around the sweating with the whole string, until you cut it all around, and make it perfect, and skin the sweating from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a ring of a dog's or iron's shape according to this form, and be subtle and draw over it:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Don't pierce him, so that he holds the two together, and presses: And if you see, cauterize the pain, as it is before or with fire-chapitre of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the ball
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one makes a ball of silver or oak wood, or melted bronze or lead; and no one makes these small or large instruments, according to the ones that are brought to them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore one should bring according to the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the ball is small and big if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say there is an opening where the belly is tied together, so that you see it, and the abdomens are pierced from within; and there is one hole on one side, and another on the other; and let the medicine be put into a bladder of cow's milk or parchment, and pierce all around each hole, and between each hole put I yard of thread, then bottie in these holes a strong thread twisted in X or thread around, and tie up the belly as if it were a sheep; and when the medicine is inside, if the instrument lies before a strong thread, then let it be clisterized; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and grease the head of the clister with oil or oak-moisture or a similar thing, then bottle it lightly; then the ministers spread themselves out their two hands together as long as he is quite dry, then remove the clister, and lift up the patient's legs against the wall, and pour out the medicine, if possible, and if he sleeps a whole night, then it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you bandage him for a disease of decay of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then remind him until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, then is the cautery also as subtle as for a child; and that is the form of the cautery subtle where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds; but we will now tell you about the treatment of hands and medicine, according to fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the hitting of a stone, and the cutting with a sword or a knife, or a lance or a staff or a spear, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that strikes on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds, for the reminder will come in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes where the bone is not broken, take care if it is from movement of stone or similar things, and the skin is indeed torn and the wound is great, and you doubt about the temp of the abscess: so do as soon as possible healing from the head itself if it comes from blood of the wound, and let the healing be in the opposite part of the wounded part; and avoid the repletion of wine and meaty food.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal, if its meat is weakened, and do not drink wine, nor eat cheese; and put on the wound, if the abscess is hot, cotton moistened with oil or wine, and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the wind, powder, which I will say a little later; and if he has moved it, put on some onions, as long as he heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as a sword-blade and similar, the lips cannot be brought together by tenderness, but if they are brought together by sutures, as I will say to the wounds of the belly, from the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And if the wound is uncovered by bone, and deep, and holds only for one patch, then cover it; but cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rust on the bone, and it has not penetrated deep enough, then cover it; but cure it with medicine, and if there is rust on an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by bandaging, then cut the artery, and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; and that you put this powder in it so that fire makes it move.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of this powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live clay three parts, and the powder finely, and apply to the wound, and bandage it together, until it heals well and joins all its blood; and then bind it firmly, and leave it untied, unless it swells; for you do not stop the medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make this of the live clay alone, unless you have incense or dragon' blood, but that fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fire has moved the wound, at least put it in this powder; but put on some herbs digested, or grains of wheat flour made with water and honey, until it dries; then heal it with other treatments as long as it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with tiny hooks; and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the neck where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the neck, if there is no other device but to let the cure take place, and not put anything restraining, for it harms the neck and makes it retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the neck is cold, and its continuation with the brain, which is the highest limb; but be the medicine sweet, as hot water washed with olive oil, and also washed with fresh water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and oiled with wet.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, so that it costs much to bind with strips, then treat until he is well.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and he is wounded and filled with bowels, and the wound penetrates or goes lower down; and if the artery is cut, and the flow of blood comes from it, and his breathing is difficult, and his throat is blocked, and his voice is hoarse, then treat him with oil; and if the pain in the throat is severe, and there is swelling, then bind it tightly, so that the meat does not touch it, but let it recover its natural shape; and then release it little by little, and leave it for a few days, and treat it with herbs until he is well; and if the wound has penetrated the bone, then seek to free it completely, and if you can't, then leave it until it putrefies and comes out on its own, and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I said in my chapter on the ointment.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the lance or sword wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	For if it is a lance or sword wound, and the wound is deep, then observe the patient: since then the wound is deadly; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh throughout all its length, then do not put the powder to him at first hour lest he vomit blood utterly, and let him lie down, and ease the pain of the patient; but apply an ointment which draws out moisture, and let him sleep on his back for three days, or four, or more; if then there will be no spasm, nor a bad quake of the body nor strangulations; and when you see that the bones are in order, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of tents and other cures, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, then make sure there is no fistula, and perform the cure accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife and is simple, deep, or at the spine, then cure it like this: if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, powder it, and if it has penetrated bone and broken into pieces, then cut the wound, and the traitors with it if they are there; and if they are not, then let the wound pus out, which will ease the extractions; and for other wounds to other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is large and medium and small; from a large wound, the intestines do not always come out, or the intestines do not enter again, so that they become swollen, sometimes freezing, so that they re-enter, and for this reason a small wound is less painful than a large one, because it takes longer for the intestines to move again; therefore, the intestines remain in place, and for this reason they swell, sometimes freezing; but as for the rupture of the abdomen, there are three ways: common sutures come from the abdominal suture, and the suture of other wounds from the trunk and other proper sutures are common with other wounds; however, they are also proper with the abdominal suture, and I will describe each one separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is nothing of the intestines out, and there is something to put back, this is done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in the third manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook it in hot water and cicero and spice, and remove the intestine as much as the swelling is relieved; and do not stop doing this, and let it rest that it may be souled to relieve.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go away, if you moisten the intestine with water or heat it and cook some vegetables, because in this way the entrance is little used; and if it cannot enter, if you make a small cut in the wound with the instrument where you cut the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to let it rest, that we do not cut it unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument to split it: if you cut it inside and turn it away, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the gut has broken loose, if you can reset it to its natural position in its own proper place, for this deserves care.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and in the lower part of the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two sides, then raise the head and chest higher than the parts below; and in this way it is necessary to treat what I have said in large and painful wounds.
