And if there is an abscess or ulcer, put something soothing on it, and let it rest for a few days; then draw out with your fingers, and be of half a thin piece of linden wood, or of a piece of palm tree, or be according to this figure: But it is necessary that the nail that you put on the break should be slightly thicker and larger than the others; and also be as far away from the limb as necessary in size; then draw on the nails as you did in the first lieure, then tie a thread to them, as you did in the first lieure on the break; the tighter it is, the better; and it is necessary that the thread is not too thick or too thin, and be of linen thread; for if the thread is too thick, like those foolish people who make their lieures with rope threads of linen, which is a great error, because the lieure cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it is only necessary that there be between each nail half an inch of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the nails of stars after extraction from their limbs, then put a pad of linen or another cloth so that he does not scar.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the seam is broken, I will tell the cure for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not fit to extract stars from all the members the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it does not fit to put stars in them but after 5 or 7 days, or more according to the severity of the abscess, hot sometimes; and here is the way of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and this is that you take flour that stays on the sides of the mill, and confound it with good amount of egg, and put this confección, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster which restores the fracture to many dispositions, and most of all to women and small children, for it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Other methods of plastering for fractures, dislocations, and torments: take honey, aniseed, onion, assafeite, gum arabic, and mugwort, 5; myrrh and aloe, 5; alchechick 8; and make a powder of them, and mix it with egg yolk from eggs; the mixture should be warm, for this plaster is good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other ways to plaster against torments: take mugwort and vismarine, 5; myrrh and aloe, 7; acacia, 6; and armatic resin, 10, grind it well, and mix it with egg yolk or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other ways to plaster against joints and bones that are out of place and relieve pain suddenly, and the size changes due to the fracture: take a new lamb, soak it in water and oil, and put it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cists do not cure, but they are good for soothing a hot abscess, and for properly treating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make an ointment that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and leaves of plantain, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an ointment for healing broken bones and for reducing the remaining swelling of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violets, flour of ash, a part of each; grind them together and confer with wine, and the limbs are warmed, confer with water and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make an ointment that is more effective than the first one, in case of a persistent abscess before healing the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of wormwood, flax seed, plantain, melilot, and stinging nettle, and violet and chamomile flowers, each part; grind them together, and confer with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not put anything on the broken member to restore it except a cerott made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things a little warm, as mirrors and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster that is good for wounds and pain: take mugwart and chamomile of the field, or feathers of owl, and vasal, and straw evenly, and grind them, and make a plaster and lay it on him.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then let him dislodge a little later, and take care that the patient feels no pain, or that his bone does not move from its place; if pain comes to its place, or pruritus, or restlessness, or swelling, hurry up and dislodge it, and dip the sponge in water, and raise the member, until the pruritus ceases, and the pain is at ease; then let him rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, wet with spring water or oil of roses, and tie it on a nut, so that you are sure of an abscess; and then continue to dislodge slightly, a little plaster, and do not squeeze it as hard as before; and to subtlety until he is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is swollen and red and painful, I have taken away all of it; and you must plaster and bind, if it returns, as you did at first to make it even.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb at all of what we have said, if it is not bound up until after three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for more than twenty days, according to what can be seen, until the break becomes tight and approaches the join of the arm on the bone; then restrain it more than before, and make the meat fat, as I said before; and if you see that it is drying up more than it needs, then wash it every day with hot water, and let it dry a little; by this work therefore cut off the bad tissue at the joint, and carefully remove what is wrong, so that the limb is straight again: this is painful, and if it is painful and fearful, and I see no other thing to do than to let it go and do it rightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are several ways of breaking, and there are different shapes and causes; for it has breaks that are made by the impact of a spear, and the collarbone is completely broken up to where it has dislocated the bone, so much as it does with the hatchet or ax; and for this is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	For the sword breaks the bone from above without piercing it, and is called  "absolute" break; and there are wounds of these great and small breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a striking inside, or an edge or collar of stone, or falling onto stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a partial break, which comes close to the membrane that is dislocated from the bone, or which is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has entered the bone as fine as an eyebrow, and is a small fracture, and so it is called this break "capillaire"; and if the wound is made or by hitting a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and thus a piece of bone enters the mouth, and the head of the cheek is broken as the blacksmith does when he strikes on the cauldron; If it goes between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And if there is more than one cheek that has moistened the bone, as the head of a child; and there are all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are broken off, like the stars; and I will talk about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and by the investigation at tents, and by the char corrupted that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is caused by the fact that when the bone is uncovered, if you rub up on it, then open the black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the break, be careful as to the accidents of the disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of reason, extension, paleness, fever, and hairs standing on end, and redness, and other similar things in many conditions, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a potentially dangerous accident, and you expect salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the birth comes first to you, and it is in winter, then you must break the bone before the fourth day at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then you must break the bone before the seventh day at most, so that the tissue surrounding the bone is not corrupted, and the accident that we have mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes only to the membrane that covers the skull, then it is necessary that you cut the broken part in this way: and it is that you press the head of the patient, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and because the blood comes at the uncovering of the bone, or abscesses, help him with whatever is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with wet towels soaked in oil; and let the wound rest as long as the abscesses are calmed, and are sure about the coming of blood; then begin to break the bone, and this is done according to II ways of work: one way is that you cut the narrow end in front, and this is its shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another way of breaking larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have many different taillemens, some short and others long, and some pointed and some of iron; and in working lightly, do not scuffle the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you pierce it inside, so that you bring taillemens with barres, not too finely so that they do not go through the bone's neck, and must be above the tip a margin or circle, so that it does not pass the tip through the bone; and you have to have more, so that each comes in its place of the end of the bone, so that you have barres for all test; and this is the form of the three ways of barres:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce inside the bone is that you put the bar in front of the bone and twist it back and forth until you know that the bone has been pierced; then remove the bar a little further away, and so do all around, and then chop the incisions the space of the bone which is between the teeth, and do it more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools that you have like tweezers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the cerebellum or the syfac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Et when you have pierced the bone and treated it, if you believe that you have removed the sharp edge of the bone from all other instruments resembling an incisors, but it is necessary that it be softer and more delicate than the other incisors; and if it does not remain attached to small bones or scales, if it breaks off lightly on the instruments; then cure the wound with tar and oils as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to cauterize is that which Galen says, which is more effective; and press it very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, where the break appears; and when you have discovered that part, you will place the tip of this lens-shaped incision there, from which it gets its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is wet in two sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then forge with a small mallet above, so that you lightly hit the bone all around, and be well guarded by the cloth that is dezos; if it is caught on the bone, then gently forge the bone, for the bone well feels harm, and no fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce just to the cloth, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, then cover again this asperity, and shave off the scales with a fine razor that you must have various quantities, to adapt in each one the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have more than one razor, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and delicate cuts, you must consider the patient's skin tone; this is something that has not been answered by those who have studied this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, then you should place a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, soaked in oil and put it on the wound; then take another cloth double-layered or triple-layered, soaked in wine and oil and put it over the first cloth; and do so more lightly than you can, so that you don't aggravate the wound, then wrap it up and don't strip it off until the abscess is completely healed; then remove it, and administer medicines as roots of herbs, and flour of fennel, and incense powder, and aniseed, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer it immediately without any stinging; and be careful that the wound stays clean, so you don't leave it with any filth, nor let anybowels assemble over the wound because when bowels gather over the wound of the skullcap, if they get torn and burst, it will cause a great deal of harm to the patient; because when you put something sharp on the wound, if it burns above it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, so that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackening does not come except because of the medicine that has been put on, which has virtue, then you should squeeze a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and make it into a ointment and apply it to the wound; then cure it in the way that seems right to you until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	I tell you that a time is never broken between the two bones above, or one alone, for they are two; and those bones are cartilaginous, and do not break unless they bend or twist, and then heal.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you should drive your little finger or pertus (a kind of bone) from the neck, and make it equal to the break with your little finger and at the back, until the neck returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain because of your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if he breaks at the top of the neck, and cannot come to his place, if you believe that you should put it equal to the head of a small ray.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if he breaks in two places, do the other way, and hurry to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscess is calm, then bind at the top of the neck with linen bandages, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind the other with the other, if he breaks; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that there is no restoration unless one softens the bandages and changes them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is right, but it is necessary that the bandages be wet with linen and mead, and dust of corn; then let the bandage rest, until the bone is hard and the cartilage has healed.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never bottle up goose feathers in the place of tents, and if there is a wind on it, and hold the broken one, and blow on the sickness among them, or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come while you are working, so that you put a cotton ball wet with oil on it, or a little patch of dyakylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come, so put an plaster on it from afar, of flour of sisarment, and powder of incense, mixed with alum of egg whites, then put it on light poultices, and do not tie the bandage; and if the dislocation of the tendon is small, and it is broken into little pieces, so extract them with suitable tools for that, then cut the tendon, and the cure of things that are injured by char, and souding, as you put plasters and oils suitable for that; and if there is no pain within the tendon, so cure the tents, and put a piece of cloth, until he is well.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the fracture is not too far off center, and it is not too badly shattered except for being a little crooked inside, then one should gently move it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side of the jaw, you should stick your index finger into the mouth of the patient from the right hand; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, stick your index finger from the left hand inside gently, and make it even, and do the same with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is on the right side in II places, then it is necessary that you bring together the two ends so that they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the inside comes from a rupture, then they should extract it with a gold or silver wire or silk thread; then put the damaged jaw on a double cloth, and put a long and wide piece of leather that is even over the jaw, and tie it to the mandible with a knot you can easily make, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, if you delay it for three days, and then put back what has been changed; and place plaster on it, of the powder from the mill with a lot of ash or flour of millet, after which you have taken off the kerite; and place on the other light plaster, and if the plaster stings, and the disposition of the sick does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times are healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come up, if you administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not take a piece of the bone out; if it is subtle to open the ostium with tools suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, if you widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have broken all these bones, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, put on it plaster suitable for this, to dry it out, as long as it is healed.
de la forcele	forcele
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force of the blow breaks it several times before, in front of the shoulder, and the break is according to three ways: or it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the overture is when the break is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds up the shoulder that is broken with force; and the others extend the neck towards the part; then make the break even on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or tangling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	Et s'il a besoin de plus grande étendue, alors mets une lance ronde de tissu, ou de laine, et soit gros selon ta nécessité; et l'étend, et le serre, et arrache la lance à ta main, de sorte que tu mettes en place la rupture, comme il convient.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the arm out at the end, so that it comes off completely, then let the patient lie down on his back, and put the shoulder under a cushion, and have someone bend the shoulder backwards, and press the shoulder blade down, until the bone comes loose.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break on both sides, and if you find it difficult to split it, then cut it with a saw; and take care not to damage the bone, and if the break is near one of the joints that you have; but put away this joint as an instrument for keeping the wound closed:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and appears like a spoon, and is not a nail, and is also wide as it should be according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has II chisels, if you see them, one is wide and the other is narrow, like the split in the wound that you made when you broke the bone; and when you are sure about the abscess being hot, if the wound splits a lot, and you doubt about the abscess being hot, then cover the wound with cloth and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, if you soak it in oil, vinegar, and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And if hot abscesses come, if you wrap it in oil, vinegar, and wine, and put it on. The extraction of the bone, when there are wounds and no fracture, is that you put plaster on the bone with powder from the mill and ash of wood, and put light strips on top, and tie a thin spine around it if you need to; then take a very thick strip one palm wide, then put double cloth on top of the strips, and plaster them; then take a thin stake three fingers wide and long, and wrap it tightly around that strip, so that the head of the strip is hanging; and put the stake over the break, and turn the strip back onto the neck, and tie the spine to the bone; and you remove each part when it gets loose, and when you see that the strip holds firmly in place, and you clearly see that the stake does not move around the bone, then you release it every day, and when the bond relaxes, if it tightens again; and make the sick person lie on his back, and put a small spine around the spine to lift the shoulder joint up; if you support the arm at the neck, and do not let any accident happen, unless there is a fracture, for 20 days; then start the plastering again, if you see that it is needed, and hold it and let it heal; and it heals in about 28 days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Here is the translation of the text:
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone comes forward, and there is no opening of the wound, then do as we have said in the breaking of the mandible to soothe an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the jaw
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The jaw bone is never broken in the middle, but this happens sometimes; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it declines towards the opening, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no support, and sometimes vomits blood, and opens the cheeks with the broken bone, and it smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lie on his back, and you place him between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and gently put them into place in all ways as you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then wrap him in plasters and seal them on top of a thin piece of wood, or other light thing, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the bone, so that it does not move; and turn the ligature around to the back, and tighten it up, and unfasten it every hour, and if it relaxes, tighten it again; and if he needs to be loosened for corruption or itching that comes to the surface, or pain or abscess, do it quickly, and loosen him, and remove the plaster, and treat it in the way of cures; then wrap the plaster back on, and tighten it up until he is well.
de la brisure des costes	of breaking the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is known that the rib breaker does not come from below the chest and back, but from within, and it does not bend much because they are stiff; and it feels right on the examination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And restore them so that you make the break even, as is appropriate.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and tie it with a strap if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib break is inward, then the patient feels great pain and stabbing, as if he were crying, because the bone rubs against the membrane; it makes him faint and vomit a lot of blood, and this is very damaging to health, and the old ones have put up with great trouble.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if for those who serve that it is appropriate to administer meat that swells the belly, so that the break goes out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, for hot poultices to come if it is not yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it be cool.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that we should put cups on the spot to draw off form, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups will not attract the excesses to the spot for the purpose of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the spot with another moist thing in oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the place equal, then it is cured of the plague, of meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain so that he cannot bear the bone that sticks out, there is doubt about the patient, then you should split the loin at the spot of the broken rib, and put a tool there to keep it away from the medicine; and then one must trim the bone, and draw it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is big, and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses arise, if they are placed on tarpaulins soaked in oil, and placed on top; and cure while the place is healing that needs an abscess, and sit gently on the costa where it is, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes that breaks the bones of the neck, and no sooner does it happen; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it has come to any person, and you can know if he will be healed or not, if you see that his hands are soft and swollen and dead, and you cannot move them or stretch them, and when you stick a needle in him, then feel the pulse.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is deadly in many dispositions, and if he mutates and feels well when they are extracted and does not feel it, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the disease is healed, if you put the cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if it seems similar, this comes to the back of the neck, and you must know whether it is healthy or not, if its muscles are relaxed, and if the accident that happened to him is in his hands, and on his back there is no will for wind and excretion; and when he is sobered on his stomach, there is no will for excretion.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is sobered on its back and it tries to get up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: do not try to work on it in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, this is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you treat him if he has an abscess, put oil or butter on it, as long as he is calm; then put on one of the poultices, and bandage it, and order the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels pain until he is healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, if necessary cover it with wool; and bind the bone, then join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, to a stitch, then dress it with ointment carrying char, until it is healthy; and if the bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow", if you hold your cup in your left hand, and put the plaster on it and put the stempel on top, if you need it; then tighten it, and if there are any bones separated, if necessary, push them together, and bind the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	the break in the leg of the horse
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	there was a little break in the leg of the horse, and if there was one, there would not be much pain at the top; and it bends, and inclines towards the ground, and causes great pain to the animal in that place, and swells up where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the setting-right is such that you extend your hand over it as long as you are above the break; and know what is the break and its form; and if the break is at the top joint, then make that break equal, as long as it remains in its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it tilts inward, then make the patient stand on his stomach, as long as the setting-right of that break has been arranged for him.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made that break equal, then put on the plaster, and then put a board of wood or of plank on it, and draw the break out, so that it does not move; and fix the joint with pins at the sides, as long as the length is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And order the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscesses come up, then do not scratch them, as long as those abscesses are calmed down, and put on that which we have mentioned above; and then return to the setting-right, and hold it as necessary, if there is no bad accident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	the dislocation of the shoulder is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then we should restore it according to one of the two ways: one is that you take a strong staff, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	and the two shoulders are tied together, and they are raised up, and he cuts the patient on a table; then he lays his arm down on the beam, so that it comes to rest, and has a piece of wood taken off; then he puts one end on any heavy object or his ministers extend it downward; then he makes the broken joint equal with his hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	and the other way is that the patient is laid on his back, and his hand is tied to his neck; then he orders his ministers that one holds what is on top of the break to his hands, and the others hold fast to all the limbs, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too strong, then tighten the thread around the break, and along the break, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the shoulder blade, then you should put the thread around the joint tightly, and along the break; and if the break is on one side of the joint, then you should tie it with a loose knot, without tension, until the break is even with the joint, and then tighten it, if necessary; and in all this work, be careful not to cause pain.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the abscess comes, then do not extract it until seven days have passed, and put a poultice on the break, then assemble the arm with the shoulder joint, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and wrap the cloth around, and extract on the joint, and on the arm, so that the arm is in the right position, if nothing hinders it, or if the bone does not break.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use a lever, and put on the break a wider and stronger bar than the others, and have between each bar two spaces, and let each bar be so large that it goes over the break III spaces from each part; then pull on the bars, so as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the paste on the break, more strongly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the bars and the pulling, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the member broken, and you doubt the aposteme warm, so leave it tied until seven days, as we have said; then look at each of the three days when the rash does not come out and go to the place, or the healing cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If done correctly, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If such an accident occurs, if no other accident happens within three or more days, and the patient sleeps on their back, with their hands on their stomach; then tie the shoulder with one piece of equal wool, and examine each hour during the day or at night, to see if the shape of the limb does not move or become looser; if it responds to medicine, and give the food we have described in a previous section, in such a way that the food is in the first layer; and when it begins to improve, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is usual that the shoulder and leg should be reset after forty days of all; and then it should be removed and bath and medicines of ointments administered to adjust it again.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if it is tight and stuck, it takes a day or two to separate.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosciles," one small and one large; the small is that which leads to the wrist, and the large is that which points towards the elbow, so that sometimes the large foscile breaks by itself, or the small, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the healing is light and good; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when it is broken together with the other.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small foscile is broken, then it is sufficient to extend it lightly and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if only the large foscile is broken, then it is necessary to stretch it more strongly; and extend it on one knee, and turn the wrist of the hand on its side higher than the other two knees, and the small fingers lower than the other two, and let the patient cross his arm over himself, and a minister's arm in front of him higher than his own arm, that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the two ministers' arms to the affected part on their side, or on their lap, and another minister's arm under them.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he should put the mirror flat, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, each one should be put in its place, and if there is any that does not hold fast, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do this on the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is an injury with the fracture, I have spoken of it to the singular chapter; take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there come abscesses, so I cover them with a cloth made of rosin oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and I cover them from above gently, until the abscesses are calm.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then cover the bone with cerott, and I put the plaster of the powder from the mill with much alum, for I put the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be close together, and one more open than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in several dispositions: whether the fracture is in one bone or in two; and draw them up more closely than elsewhere, and always less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter of the plaster; and let the cloths that are on the fracture be soft and wet, and let not be hard nor rough; and let the thread, from which it is drawn, be of linen, not too thick nor too fine, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And keep the limb and the ligature for several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, it is necessary that you dunk the member in hot water until this itching is calmed; and let the member not be strained to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again with extraction, and if the ligature is softened and the bone broken, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the member cannot be moved because it is too stiff, then you must soften it a little and leave it for several days until the rigor is gone, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, do not remove the ligature until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or, let him hold his hands by his neck, and make his necks equal, and guard against movement and stirring, and lie on his back; and know that this healer is healed in thirty days or twenty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and on our two sides there are few breaks, and there comes but a little pain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or painful, so that the patient cries out, and sits upright equally before him; then he lays his hand on a spread cloth, and spreads the broken bones, and makes them equal, as they are well joined; and lays the plaster and bandages, if there comes an abscess, then he puts a stake according to the quantity of space; and let it be wrapped up in one draping of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks within the parchedens between the belly of the plant, make a rope of drapels, and instruct the patient that he strangle it to his broken plant; and then extract it with a long rope, and his steel of curd is as great as the plant of the hand, and extract it, if so it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks at the back, if it is convenient that you put a steel on, and another dislocated in the plant so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and stop the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if it breaks at one of the two, if it is pulled out, then make it even, as it should be; and pull it with the plant, and if you see that one puts a small straight steel to raise the break, so that it does not move; and if the break is on the other two, as in the index or one of the others, make it even, and tie them together holding them tight, so they do not move, or you put them on a steel, as if a pouchet; and take care with the restoration and proper position of the aposteme, and help those who come after, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the chest's wound
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the chest are often bruised, and it is clearly seen when they turn in front and behind; and the healing is done if they are tied above and below thebruise.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each minister his ligature to its equal part; and it is when the bruise has entered into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the bruise is close to the root of the chest, so be one of the ligatures towards the knuckle, and the other ligatures below thebruise.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the knee, so be one of the ligatures towards the knee, and the other ligatures below thebruise; then put the hammer the bone according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and the ligatures, since there is no pain.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it be soothed then return to your work and your cure; the time is right in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess, let it be soothed then return to your work and your cure; the time is right in this way.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	Et s'il arrive, s'il tombe, et retient ce qui est venu, s'il arrive comme nous l'avons souvent dit; et s'il y a des morceaux d'os qu'il tient, s'il peut, s'il ne peut pas, s'il faut le faire voler, et le tirer fort; et le guérir comme nous l'avons dit, jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And if he falls, and holds what has come, if it arrives as we have often said; and if there are pieces of bone that he holds, if he can, if he cannot, if he has to break the place, and pull hard; and heal him as we have said, until he is healed. And never is the belly injured in such a way that one puts pads on it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in such a restoration made, the patient does not become ill.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the belly is restored in 24 hours, or less or more, according to the diversity of tempers.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	I understand that in the knee joint there may be a slight crack, but it often leaks many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, there is only a crack, or a dent, and if there is a hole, and if there is no pain, and this hurts less.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the repair is that one put even what is long in two, as much as it can be held; then apply the ointment and put a round bandage on it, if you need it, and tighten it as we have said in other breakages, such as a hot burn and another injury; put on each accident whatever belongs to it, until he is well.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	I understand that there are two bones in the leg, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; it has all the same fractures as the arm, and the repairs are also the same. If both bones break together, the leg will twist on itself.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his small bone is broken, then turn him around.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if his big bone is broken, then feel the pain and see it clearly; and turn away.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then bring it out, and make it even, and tie the joints evenly; but nonetheless, his fracture is ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter; and align it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two hair braids that purple the leg on one side and the other, and are long at the leg from the ankle up; then wrap them both around above and below, and tie them in the middle, and so it cannot move either to the right or to the left, and so is good; and no one administer two braids of long hair, and if it's red, and put the leg to keep it from moving, and properly done this on the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident; then cure as long as it is well.
de la brisure des os dou piet	about the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture at all, but at the foot there is sometimes a fracture and in some cases only a crack, and in many cases it is only a break.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a fracture in the foot, and you see these bones protrude one above the other, so that the person can barely stand on the ground, like they want to walk, then now put your foot on their side, where the bones are raised, then press them until they go back into their places; then apply the plaster and cover it, and put a small tray of two flat boards at the front of the foot, then tie it to the foot with strips, and other things that you need.
