Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three days or four have passed, if the swelling has gone down, because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there is any of the two broken, if you restore them, as we have said to the hands of the man; then put on the broken one a stone according to its length of the two, and let it be a little wider, then fasten at its base that which I have said, and strain forward; and if there are II or III, or more, broken, put on each of the two a stone according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen drape, and strain out the slush at the base of the foot; and let it be while it is on the top of the slush far from the foot, so that he shades it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about the other breakages, as soon as we have said; and heal each accident as it should be healed.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the arm bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the woman's natural neck is broken, if she is made to sit enlarged, then lean her to the back part, and be held behind; then fill the nature of the illness with cotton, and put in it as big as I stand; then take off the woman, and lift up her back little by little, and then cut the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the neck with the stand; and when she wants to urinate, if she cuts the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back again, and do so for seven days or more: she will be healed, and you shall see. Then take a bladder of lamb, and tie a rope around the navel, and pour all the bladder into nature; then blow into the rope, forming until the bladder is inside: nature will then heal the break; then fill it with cotton, and let it be like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	Et when the bone of the arm is broken, or of the woman, so that it returns as we have said about the bone of the thigh; and these breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and use to it, and hears my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means many things to the right way of restoration: hear it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the vagina, when it is broken, take a goose neck and pour into the vagina; then wrap with a cloth, and leave for III days or longer, and it will be healed in hospital.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	To him who has a break with a wound, especially if it is great, as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, let it be healed now, so that the wounds that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, if the vitriol remains, then you don't have anything else, then start to restore the break in this same hour, or if it is a morning wound, then if the abscesses don't come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses come, if you don't restore it until the next day, as long as the abscesses are calmed down, and you don't touch them on the third day or the fourth, because you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is exposed on the side that has been cut, then you must put it at a slight angle with your hands, gently and little by little.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not aligned so that your hands are equal in length, then take this iron instrument, which has seven or eight inches of length, and make it wide according to the quantity of the wound; and for this one is skilled in the mire that it takes III or IV, according to what it needs in each cure of a broken limb; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member with your work, and be sharp in front, and thick in the middle:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because it is necessary that the bent head be placed on top of the highest point of the bone; and it should be stretched once, as long as it returns, and even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot take the bone well, you must knock the head of the bone until the instrument has the power to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back together, as we have said, using a suitable instrument, either an incision or a file, within your power; then remove that which is stuck in the bone with roughness and small scrapes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone has been put back together, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its place, then soak the wound with red wine and let it sit properly; and do not put on the wound wax or any other oil where there is oil, lest it cause corruption and putrefaction; then apply plaster when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and give yourself well in mind that the wound should not be constricted with the break; and many times this has happened, and it has brought about death or corrupting the patient sometimes; and the extractions are softer and milder than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is bad or large and you doubt that good accidents will come, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, then it does not suit you to put on plasters; but wrap, instead of plasters, hard wraps, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days to enter Bowen in the wound, if it is what you have put up all win, and I put healing ointments, as ointment tetrafarmasion and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is fixed and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the Bowen runs down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it is a day passing, and he cannot fix but comes together Bowen, his bones, because there are little pieces of bone that come out of place, so you must mend the wound with a patch, and all these wrong pieces that come out cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if there is a fistula coming to light, or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he said in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the jaw is broken, and opened on the side of the member, as the jaw of the cheek or shoulder, and other large members, let it not be pulled out, for many times death comes, but leave it to putrefy; perhaps after XX days or XXX, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The bruses that come from سودرة
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	come again after the health of the rupture, especially when it is near the joint, and an ugly thing is to see the figure of the member; and perhaps cannot make the members do their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore if we are fresh: if you administer sticky medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcacollus, acacia, and similar ones, so that you do not press any of these things, or all together, and confound them with wine of aloes or with a lot of ash or with mustard; and put them on the knot in piles, and bind them well, and do not remove them in hand days; and then loosen it, and start another one, as long as the knots are hard; or you hold it on a piece of leather well made; for the property of leather is that it hardens all swelling on the members; and if the knot has already become hardened, it is necessary to cut it off, and let it be apparent; or you take it to any barber, as long as it is hardened, and cure it until it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after imprisonment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and the weak and fine limbs remain due to various causes: either because he was too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bands, and could not bring the member into position; or because of a lot of inflammation; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because he had little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until there is an increase of blood in him; and give him bath, and provide joy and rest; then put poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts the great nourishment, and dampens it often with warm water, until the nourishment goes to the member; and come back to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two damaged limbs after surgery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after healing, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, however, it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that the member must be broken anew, and many such fools have done this in our land; these practices are blamed, and great harm and perhaps death result; yet, if the nodules and torments are fresh, it is good that they be boiled in warm water, or soft herbs are cooked, as fern leaves of whale blubber, and roots, and mellilot, and similar things; and the salve made with a mild ointment, such as well-made hydronium, and you take the musk of whale blubber, and confound it with lard or oil of sesame seed, and make a salve; or you take fat figs, and grind them with hay of coles, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the neck bent by constantly rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement in each limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the stiffness is great and hard, as in stone, it must be opened by the iron, somewhat lightly, with a gentle incision; and put a covering and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it can be brought back without hurting.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, and the limbs increase in swelling, and by chance he is put back into place at his own pace; for then spams and other pains often come; however, when this happens, the sick person must be made well, then leave it, until the abscesses are calm; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then move it slightly, and heal each member as the disease comes;
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chaplets of dislocations of the shoulder joint just up to the foot.
des mandibules	the mandible
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	And let the mandible be dislocated little by little, and the dislocation of both is according to two ways: either they are a little bone-broken from their places, and a little softened; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the loin, and stop the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is little, so return by them several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, so that you reset it quickly, and do not tarry at all; and in such a way that the ministers hold the head of the sick person, and pour some medicine from one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, so that the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands should be away, to make it even; and order the patient that he softens his jaws, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he marks the met to be equal, as long as it regains its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And he brings it back with care, especially if both jaws are together, and by hot water and oil, as gently as possible; do not delay bringing it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back in equal measure, and the mouth of the sick person closes well with mild softener, if placed on drapings wetted with a paste made of oil and wax, then let it lie gently; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two pillows so that he does not move from side to side or make any effort to improve, but eat lightly, until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; and then drink and eat as desired, and do not worry about opening the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and usual heat come, and by chance a solution of the stomach, and by chance vomit of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times dies he who has it, in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	cannot be dislocated from within the jaw over time and from the back of the tongue, and is dislocated several times to the side; and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the sick person lies on his back and extends his arms; then press the joint with your palm, and it will come back; then put the plaster and bandage on it, and bind it, and instruct the patient that he should rest as long as he is not well; and in this way is also reset the head of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	I understand that the shoulder can dislocate in three ways: either it comes out of its socket; or out of the chest; perhaps out of the top, which is bad; and never out of the back, nor into the neck; and many times it comes out of the socket towards the arm, but at those who have little strength, it happens that they do not notice anything, and go on their way; and those who have enough strength, they notice a little bit, and come back to their normal state.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes there was percussion or breaking in men; and the shoulder was hot from an abscess, and they thought it had dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary therefore that you test it, until you are sure of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tocier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaleee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tocier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift up the hand of the sick person above, then put on gloves off the arm, and push the joint up with force in place; and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it above, then put it back; so come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said above, in the hands of days after, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and provide soothing and relaxing vapors, as an infusion of althea and fenugreek and melilote in water, and be administered; then let the patient lie on his back, and remove the shoulder brace a little from one side, not too soft or too hard, then put the mirror on the heel of the foot on the stand, and gently lift up the shoulder with care, and pull the hand of the patient; and other ministers wipe the head of the patient, so that it does not move downward; this shoulder returns all at once, and if you do it in this way: it is that you make a man present who is more than the patient; and let him stand on his back, and bottle up the shoulder from the brace of the patient, and lift up the brace above, so that the patient hangs in the air; and other ministers pull the hand of the patient downward towards his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then with him put something heavy, so that the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And let him put on also in another way: and is it stuck a long splinter in the earth, from which the shoulder is also reason as a pistol, and is not too thick or too light; then is put out to the lou malade, but that he has drapels suet over, and the malaied is standing on the long stick of the fuse; then is extended his hand down another side forming, and the jointure will return to its place permanently; and if it does not return by all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a splinter from the arms of great and IIII fingers wide, which has the head reont for perfectly enter in asselle according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	And then put it on the top of the long splinter suet drapels, so that the fuse does not hurt the lou malade, then put it in asselle the lou malade; and extends his arms up the long stick, and puts the ajutoire on the stick, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on a peg of a shelf wide, and let the hands down, and let the body hang from another part: the jointure will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in any way, it is necessary that you put on the shoulder an equal piece of wool, then place the plaster prepared from powder from the mill, with incense and oil of olive, all over the shoulder and armpit, and then remove the shoulder as if dislocating it, and tie it back to the plaster, and embrace the hand around the neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he suck for a little while, until the members are comfortable, because he will heal faster; and then suck after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and has not become soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or some other cause, it is necessary that you apply the cauterization three times, as it is put before or with the paste of the cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it slides after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm forward, then know that the nerves in the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint has never been properly set in place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation that is around the neck and shoulders, or behind, so it is made by impact, stretching of hands, and I place it in another location; and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the cure comes greasiness to the member, and delayed motion, then use the patient many times, as long as that greasiness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated to the ends, and returns to the ends; and if it is dislocated from all sides, most of all in front and behind, and the dislocation is not properly set, for it can be seen and felt well; and desolate according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the sound one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it so that the abscesses are cut as they should, for if the abscesses are cut, then it would be painful to reset it; and by chance it cannot be reset from all sides at all, especially when it is behind; this one hurts more than the others, and often leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is so, when it is such that you can reset it, that you extend its hand with your two hands; and its arms are spread out, and its hands turn in towards the back according to the neck at the center, away and back, and press the joint into its sockets together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and proud of the root of the palm foot that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, then administer a strong extension; and it is that the two ministers extend the arm, and they dip them in water, so that he does not move in the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when you see the joint joined to his hand, then oile it with any oil to soften the joint, then put the joint together, until it returns; and when it is in its place, then lay it on dry plaster with sheep's fat, and strain it together, and bend the arm at the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen it and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not fit well, then recommence the plastering and bonding and leave it for a few days, as long as it is firmly fixed; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels cold after the joint has been moved, and the joint moves, then bathe and gently rub it, and press until it is relieved; or you put on the joint a thin layer of fat sheep's wool, then leave it for a day and a night, then make the bone, and let it enter or bathe; and when it sweats, rub the joint quickly, then put the wool back on, and then enter or bathe; and do this II times or III, until it is healed; and if you see, then put on a piece of wet sheep's skin that has been warmed with butter, and stretch it over; if it returns to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand is reversed, and the return is lighter than that of other joints However, it must be returned to its place urgently during movement so that the joint does not move, or a hot abscess may develop.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you bring it back, put the injured hand on a table, and extend its fingers, and make them equal so that its palm is facing the joint, and keep them extended until it returns to its place However, it is necessary for you to check if it is well placed; then put the back of the hand on a table for extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the back of the hand of the patient on a table, and make him extend his fingers so that his palm faces the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If she comes back now, it is well; if not, if the extraction of pus-filled abscesses leaves her in this state, then she will continue to feel pain.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it and you cannot set the joint after a few days, then the joint will remain twisted; nor does there exist any remedy for the patient except to extract by means of a delicate cautery, or perhaps there is no other remedy than to cut off the nerve or artery by a delicate cautery, and perhaps there is no other remedy. Do you know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries? If so, then he should be operated on immediately; if not, he will die.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have described; then extract it and leave it for 5 days, then remove it and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move it well, and there is no crack, then the warm water, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two joints in the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	If there is no dislocation of the two joints in the hand at either end, nor on the back of the palm or on the belly; then they are joined again, and press down the dislocation toward the pockets until it comes back, then hold the knuckle of the joint, and turn it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for a day, and then make it even that day; and if necessary, let it rest, so as to move it again, and tie it up; and do this often, until it is tight, and do likewise, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and likewise, if it is dislocated from another end.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Dou desaluement de l'eschinee dou dos.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck or shoulder is dislocated, or several are dislocated, if there is no cure, for the patient will quickly die.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs that it is are that the expulsions jump without will, cannot be held, and often a member becomes soft, or the two legs or the two arms or one; and often the eschinee mutates in four parts; that which mutates to the rear is called "gilbositez": if there is no cure for it, or no improvement, for all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting down or percussion or similar things, the ancient ways of treatment with big words did not do any good at all; but I have simplified them according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	Je dis que en la gilbosité que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre formant
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	I say that in the giddyenness that comes before the pit, there is no help or cure; and also what comes straight on both sides, and cannot be cured except that which comes properly from behind, as I have said; and it is that the patient lies flat on his back in an even position, and has the strain taken away from him so that he does not bleed; then put a hot coal at the head resting on the ground, and another between the feet, and tie a rope around the patient's shoulders, and another between the knees, and ankle bones; and two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other between the feet, among the two coals; and they are well secured, the coal as we have said, and the minister puts his palms on the spine resting on the ground, until he recovers.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Et est that you stick II torches to the head of the patient with an arm long, and between the torch II others, and have between each torch, above and below, a palm of space long; and have in each torch I perforation, or the twist corre, and let the torch firmly in the ground so that it does not move; and between each II torches have II turning torches because the bond turns, and have in II twists II small torches of a palm long, to turn the twist; and then he binds the bond that is among the hands at the twist towards the head, and the other bond towards the torch with the other twist, and each helper twists his bond on all the bond, and the master puts the needle even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, so put on dried plaster with much blood-root, and then the stumps, and then the stake of a tablet of III quarters long, that by propering the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine healthy, then bind with a bond as we have said, and use the patient with subtle fasting until he is healthy; and if anything comes at the end of health, so administer medicines softening and soothing, with the stake that we have said before; and never give one piece of limestone, and never does the appearance come in the rear spine of the back, and take care that it is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, for he should not have presumption: by adventure might come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	I understand that hip and shoulder dislocations occur only in specific ways, unlike other joints, and that the hip joint has four dislocation directions: internal and external, front and back, with the internal direction being the most critical.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocations within is that when we join the injured leg with the healthy one, it is further away, and the patient's knees are higher than the healthy ones, and the patient cannot double his knee when he stands; and it is this distance that is swollen with an abscess, because the hip joint comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those to whom it happens in back is that this accident is opposite to these in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those to whom it happens in front are that their leg is well arranged according to the proportions; however, they cannot double their knee without pain, and when they are made to walk, they cannot go forward, and they hold their urine back, and their ankels swell, and when they walk, they go on their heels.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is behind, if he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the hip joint is soft, and the thigh bone is in its place between the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And those who have this appearance of dislocation if they do not move it, and this leg is more bent than the other, and the hip joint is soft, and the thigh bone is in its place between the ribs. Remind them of this appearance of dislocation if they do not heal quickly, according to their condition, for there is no cure; and it is not right that he should be confident.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is recent, and it is of the four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to reset the joint, and turn it inside out and outside in, and move it from side to side; perhaps it will come back, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, it is necessary that you prepare the minister very strongly, and support the leg very firmly with two hands, or with a bandage whatever it may be tied to the knee; and extend another minister his hand above and below in such a way that he presses his hands against his knees, then tie him by a strap across the chest; and extend them all at once, so that the patient is raised from the ground all at once, and remain still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This way of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to treat his appearance when the dislocations are at rest, as we will say, that you put the patient on his back with care, then put the bandage on the root of the groin, and the strap that is away from the angle, then extend the bandage upwards towards the angle, and towards the force; then grasp the arms of the minister, and embrace the large strap of the groin of the patient, and extend it away in this way: if it returns to its place now; and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Et si tu ne peux pas serrer ainsi comme nous avons dit, alors il convient que tu lices les deux pieds du malade ensemble d'un fort lien souef sur les deux talons, et sur les deux genoux, et soit la jambe malade étendue de deux côtés plus que l'autre; puis soit pendu au haut d'une poutre, et soit sur le sol deux bras longs; puis commande à un ministre qu'il embrasse la tête de la cuisse, et soient autres ministres pendans avec le malade, qui embrassent forment la cuisse, car le jointure revient maintenant hospitalement.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And if the dislocations are away, then lay the patient down as we have said in that which has gibbosity, and extrude the bandage properly on the leg which is disabled, and also on the foot; then place two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a torch between the legs of the disabled person toward his back; and plant wet drapes around, so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each minister away from him, and let the patient put his hand in equal position to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on .ie a table, and press it in as we have said in the gibosity, and place the patient on the right side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are forward, if it is necessary to extend the leg of the patient in bed, and according to what I have said; and put the mirror so that its pain is above the sore knee, then press with the other hand, and turn it sideways towards the foot.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are on the side, if it is not necessary to extend the leg of the patient in bed, nor to lift him up from the ground, but rather that he should be placed on his back as if he were lying on his stomach; and be on his face, and the limb be extended as we have said above, and press on the joint at the table; and it will be done when the leg is extended and they are even; then set the splint, and put the plaster, and stretch it with a bandage, so that the leg does not move; and rest for three or four days, then take off the splint, and make him walk as best he can, until the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and behind; and does not dislocate before.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place his back on his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his kneecap with your palms, and pull between your two hands, then bend the II ribs of the knee cap together; and others extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that he bends his leg at the knee easily; and put the plaster on, and make him raise his leg at the knee, and join them firmly for III days or IIII, then let it go; and do not work on the patient's going away, until the members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in their place, give a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healed
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation from the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are neither dislocated nor completely shifted, and inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and lean forward to the part where it has been shifted: one should gently bend it with their hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from the top, you should make the patient lie down right side up, and support the leg by the thigh; then treat the foot with your hand on your own side, and then do the same with the other side, and then extend it upwards, and blow hard on the foot; and do this twice, as we have said, by blowing and treating the foot; if it returns, it is good; but if not, begin again with the work, for it will return; and if it does not return thus, so make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place the staff firmly in the ground between his knees, and tie up the sheets so that he does not fall forward; then turn the minister round who is holding the thigh, and others extend the foot equally with their hands or legs, so as to keep it still; then the minister who is holding the dislocated part should hold it in place with his hands, and others support the healthy leg by the shin; then the dislocation will come back all right.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is hard, then put on the plaster and press down on it, and form the strain, and fasten the leg to the foot, and guard the tendons behind the ankle, so that the ties are not too tight; then let it alone for two or three days, and the ties will become soft if the strain remains; then release it on the third day or fourth, and send the sick person away after four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he has not dislocated again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come up, then it is necessary that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, as long as they are healthy.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, then it is necessary to extend them smoothly without work, and that is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are in no part of the foot's joint, then it is necessary that you make the sick person sit on a level plain or table all straight, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press against your foot forming, until he recovers; and when it is even, and there is no opening, then set aside the sole of the foot on a table with II chairs, then form the strain, and let it alone for three days, then release it; and cause him to rest, until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and it needs to be restored, many times the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, do not be ignorant in the art and have not used it long enough, and do not be proud, compassionate, and tardy; use at the beginning things that calm the abscess, and leave the patient to God, unless you see a chance of health; and when you see a chance, now put the member back in place, so that the abscesses come out; and when the member is in place, administer dry things to the abscess, and cure the wound as it should be, with ointments; and if there is a break with dislocation, and small bones are broken, set them, and do what we have said for simple illnesses; and guard yourself from entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will cost you much according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming yourself and your body.
Amen	Amen
